    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1632025206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1632025206" />
    <a title="Anastasia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29194167-anastasia"><img alt="Anastasia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459611514p2/29194167.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1632025206?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anastasia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anastasia" href="/user/show/29194167-anastasia">Anastasia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18115294-this-song-will-save-your-life">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1632025206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13107984033212728104"><i> <b> 5/5 stars </b> </i><br/><br/><i> <b> Trigger Warnings: suicide, self harm, depression, bullying </b> </i><br/><br/><i> Elise Dembowski doesn’t fit in. She spends the summer before her sophomore year of high school literally studying pop culture: the celebrities, the styles, the popular music. She hates it all, especially the saccharine, auto-tuned music. When it comes to music, Elise has standards. But she has come to the conclusion that, had she been more normal as a young child, she wouldn’t have become such an outsider. It may be too </i></span>
  <span id="freeText13107984033212728104" style="display:none"><i> <b> 5/5 stars </b> </i><br /><br /><i> <b> Trigger Warnings: suicide, self harm, depression, bullying </b> </i><br /><br /><i> Elise Dembowski doesn’t fit in. She spends the summer before her sophomore year of high school literally studying pop culture: the celebrities, the styles, the popular music. She hates it all, especially the saccharine, auto-tuned music. When it comes to music, Elise has standards. But she has come to the conclusion that, had she been more normal as a young child, she wouldn’t have become such an outsider. It may be too late to change her fate now, but she has to try. On the first day of school, she pulls on her skinny jeans and a tee shirt with a flattering neckline, slides a headband into her hair (the magazines say that headbands are in), and stands at the bus stop. Still, no one talks to her. But it’s early in the day, right?<br /><br />When a final attempt at popularity fails, Elise nearly gives up. Then she stumbles upon a warehouse party where she meets Vicky, a girl in a band who accepts her; Char, a cute, yet mysterious disc jockey; Pippa, a carefree spirit from England; and most importantly, a love for DJing. </i><br /><br /><blockquote> <b> <i> “You think it’s so easy to change yourself. You think it’s so easy, but it’s not.” </i> </b> </blockquote><br />When I first heard about this book I was completely sold. The summary hit a little too close to home but I knew that if I ever got my hands on this book it would change my life. Once I saw a couple reviews and videos about how amazing the book was on youtube, especially Emmmabooks (If you are reading this. Thank you so much for raving about this book and promoting it to your audience. This book has truly changed my life for the better and like the title states it will “save your life”.), I had to pick it up; and I am so glad that I did. <blockquote> <b> <i> “Sometimes when you are worn down, day after day, relentlessly, with no reprieve for years piled on years, sometimes you lose everything but the ability to cry.” </i> </b> </blockquote> Elise is a sophomore in High School and has never really fit in with her peers. But she wants to change this. She wants to sit in the middle of the bus instead of the front, have someone sit with her instead of sitting alone, have a conversation with someone instead of listening to her ipod. Feeling like you don’t belong has been a general feeling amongst the youth of today; especially High Schoolers. Being a High School student myself I really connected to what Elise was feeling and all of the thoughts going through her head. Once Elise decided she had had enough of the bullying and abuse she was receiving at school she decided to hurt herself. After cutting herself she realized that she didn’t want death she just wanted someone to care if she died. A couple months, therapy sessions, hospital visits later Elise is back in school and stumbles across an underground nightclub and she comes alive. <blockquote> <b> <i> “I like projects where I could take things apart and figure out exactly how they worked. The problem is, you can’t do that with people.” </i> </b> </blockquote> Elise meets many people while at the nightclub. Mel, the guard/body guard at the door of the club who becomes a father figure for Elise. Vicky, an outgoing soon to be rockstar who befriends Elise. Pippa, Vicky’s “do now ask later” kind of friend. Char, the Start’s DJ and mentor to Elise. Every single character in this book had depth, even the petty popular girls in school that we only meet for a couple of pages. They were all interesting and unique. There were a few stereotypes used throughout the book but it helped convey Elise’s thoughts and how she sees High School. <blockquote> <b> <i> “I was smiling like a crazy person because I had just made a hundred people dance, I had just made a hundred people scream, I had just made a hundred people happy.” </i> </b> </blockquote> Char, the DJ at Start, sees Elise’s love of music and talent with the turntables. He takes her under his wing and teaches not only how to DJ but how to DJ the right way. It’s not only about playing songs that you like over and over. Anyone with an ipod can do that. It’s about reading the crowd to see what they are reaction to, beat matching, and most of all losing yourself in the feel of the music. Elise is a fast learner and soon Char lets her DJ for a half hour every night on Thursday’s. Elise loves the feeling of being in the DJ booth looking out over the club and watching what her music can do to people. In those moments she is truly happy, but when the lights turn on and she has to sneak back into her bedroom, the feeling of being invincible starts to fade. <blockquote> <b> <i> “Tonight the Internet seemed filled with versions of me, like a fun house filled with mirrors. Some of them made me look prettier, and some of them made me look uglier, and some of them chopped me right in half, but none of them were right.” </i> </b> </blockquote> Elise loves the nightclub scene. When the lights are dim and the music is loud everything looks ten times better and everyone seems ten times more interesting. That bartender? He is a college student trying to pay for his schooling. That girl with the shirt skirt and spiky pumps? She’s a talented singer that’s trying to graduate. That DJ with the unicorn boots? She’s a sophomore in High School that’s bullied and is just trying to fit in. But in the dark you don’t see all of these insecurities or normal features of a person. You only see what they want you to see, because for one Thursday night every week they can be whomever they want. <blockquote> <b> <i> “Sometimes you just have those days. When you know, from the moment you wake up, that everything you touch you will break, so the less you touch, the better.” </i> </b> </blockquote> This book is one of the best portrayals of depression, anxiety, and bullying I have ever read. From the first page I was sucked into Elise’s head and found myself engulfed in emotion. For me this book put all of my feelings, fears, and insecurities on paper and it was a little sad and hard to read. But, in the end this book helped me come to terms with those feelings and ultimately helped me understand myself better. <blockquote> <b> <i> “Sometimes you just have those days where everything goes wrong. But sometimes, and totally unexpectedly, something can go right.” </i> </b> </blockquote> This book shows that even when you feel like everything is broken, one day with help, everything will come back together. Each person’s feelings and emotions are valid, and every situation is different. This means that reading this book you might feel the portrayal of depression, etc isn’t good because that wasn’t your or a loved one's experience. But, somewhere out in the world there is someone reading this book and connecting to the characters feelings and finding a sense of understanding and love in between these pages. <blockquote> <b> <i> “I was giving up. But sometimes you have to give up something you are to get to who you want to be.” </i> </b> </blockquote> The writing style was perfect. It was just descriptive enough to imagine the scene but vague enough that you could modify certain things. Leila Sales’ writes amazing characters and plot. There weren’t any lagging moments or scenes that weren’t vital to the growth of characters or the plot. <blockquote> <b> <i> “It was a very small compliment, but it came from someone who mattered, about something that mattered.” </i> </b> </blockquote> All in all if you are in the right mindset this book will move you. Elise is a relatable character that burrowed into my heart, read my mind, and spoke to my soul. Her words didn't seem overplayed or fake. All she wanted to be was popular and you know what happened instead? People were horrible and treated her badly. Some say it's the "high school experience", but to me that's just an excuse for the abuser. It doesn't matter if it's verbal, physical, emotional, cyber, or in person, what matters is that one person is being hurt. I absolutely loved this book and it definitely holds a special place in my heart. <br /><br />Mental illness is not something we should look over. It may be scary to speak or even think about but if you are feeling depressed, suicidal, anxiety, or are suffering from abuse, bullying, or any other crises please talk to someone, visit the websites below, or call a helpline. Please reach out to someone who can help.<br /><i> <b> United States Suicide Hotlines:</b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.suicide.org/suicide-hotlines.html">http://www.suicide.org/suicide-hotlin...</a><br /><b> International Suicide Hotlines:</b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.suicide.org/international-suicide-hotlines.html">http://www.suicide.org/international-...</a><br /><b> 24 Hour Crisis Hotline:</b> (212) 673-3000<br /><b> National Domestic Violence Hotline:</b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.thehotline.org/">http://www.thehotline.org/</a> <br /><b> For many more crisis hotlines such as depression, suicidal thoughts, stress, anxiety, grief, bullying, and so much more: </b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.teenhealthandwellness.com/static/hotlines">http://www.teenhealthandwellness.com/...</a> </i> <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13107984033212728104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1290813827" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1290813827" />
    <a title="Chelsey Connor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43438271-chelsey-connor"><img alt="Chelsey Connor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549517917p2/43438271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1290813827?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsey Connor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsey Connor" href="/user/show/43438271-chelsey-connor">Chelsey Connor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43438271-chelsey-connor?shelf=music">music</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43438271-chelsey-connor?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43438271-chelsey-connor?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43438271-chelsey-connor?shelf=covers-i-love">covers-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43438271-chelsey-connor?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43438271-chelsey-connor?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43438271-chelsey-connor?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43438271-chelsey-connor?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1290813827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5028932525980163257">I really enjoyed this book. I was expecting something completely different actually. The struggles Elise went through happen so often in our world today and I just loved seeing how everything did turn out great in the end. She pushed through and found a great bunch of friends and found something that she loved and brought her so much joy.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1455339491" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1455339491" />
    <a title="Anne " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23304719-anne"><img alt="Anne " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564193777p2/23304719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1455339491?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne " href="/user/show/23304719-anne">Anne </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23304719-anne?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23304719-anne?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23304719-anne?shelf=self-discovery">self-discovery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23304719-anne?shelf=adorable-little-brothers">adorable-little-brothers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23304719-anne?shelf=school-setting">school-setting</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1455339491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12744128175793688664"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> I was born to be unpopular.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><b>Let me start out </b>this review by painting you pictures.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>PICTURE 1 </u>
</b><br/><b>Elise Dembowski </b>has always been unpopular, there was never a moment when it wasn't so, there was no such thing as pinpointing the <i>exact</i> moment which marked her fall from grace. And I hereby submit these quotes as irrefutable evidence:<br/><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>"Don't be special." That's what I would say to my younger self if I could pinpoint the moment when I went astray. But there was no one moment. I was a</i></blockquote></b></span>
  <span id="freeText12744128175793688664" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> I was born to be unpopular.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><b>Let me start out </b>this review by painting you pictures.<br><br><b>
  <u>PICTURE 1 </u>
</b><br><b>Elise Dembowski </b>has always been unpopular, there was never a moment when it wasn't so, there was no such thing as pinpointing the <i>exact</i> moment which marked her fall from grace. And I hereby submit these quotes as irrefutable evidence:<br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>"Don't be special." That's what I would say to my younger self if I could pinpoint the moment when I went astray. But there was no one moment. I was always astray.<br><br>And then one day on the playground, Lizzie Reardon came over and casually said to my new friend, “Don’t spend too much time with Elise. She might rub off on you.” I was sitting right there. It wasn’t a secret. I was a social liability.<br> This was fourth grade. <br><br> I’ve gone to school with the same kids since kindergarten. And they knew what I was long before I did. I was uncool by fourth grade. How is it even possible to be an uncool fourth grader? Didn’t we all just string together friendship bracelets and daydream about horses and pretend to solve mysteries back then?<br> But somehow, even in fourth grade, they knew. </i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><b>Elise is sixteen now.</b> And nothing has changed, if anything, things have only gotten worse.<br>The long and short of it?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451364779ra/17533686.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>PICTURE 2</u>
</b><br>We have now been acquainted with Elise's sad and unfortunate fate. Next thing to know is, that all her life, all she ever wanted was to be accepted, to be liked, to not be herself. <b>To not be special. </b> She's so fixated on these thoughts and wishes that whenever a hand of kindness(no matter how glaringly and evidently wolfish and dishonest it is) is extended to her by the most unlikely people, she becomes erroneously gullible and falls prey to their lies. Every single time. She's so broken down and worn out that she can't fight back, can't stand up for herself, not once. So she's been swallowing crap her whole life.<br>The long and short of it? <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451325597ra/17528207.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451364779ra/17533687.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451364779ra/17533688.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And all the while, I'm rolling around in my bed, yelling:<b> DON'T FREAKING EAT THE POISONED APPLE! DON'T FREAKING EAT IT!!!</b><br><br><b>
  <u>THE REST OF THE STORY LINE</u>
</b><br><b>The year before </b>Elise became a sophomore, she <b>
  <u>pretended </u>
</b> to attempt suicide(I promise there are no spoilers at all, it all happens within 8-10% of the book) Attempted meaning - Of course, she failed. So we have our heroine a year later still struggling to keep up with life. Still trying to live, or rather cope. One day she comes across an abandoned warehouse night club named <b>Start,</b> where she meets people who will later on influence her life, people who, like her, know and understand the power of music.<br><br><b>
  <u>MY THOUGHTS</u>
</b><br>I'm going to say, that it pains me greatly to rate this book the way I did. I have a deep and great respect for books(and authors), like this, that address important and crucial subjects which plague the society. Most especially, those that explore pertinent questions pertaining to the topic of rape, sexism, bullying and ostracism. There's just <b>too much</b> emphasis placed nowadays on fitting into a particular image, a mould which society deems as <b>norm, acceptable, and conventional.</b> One of the many manifestations of such pressure on people-teenagers mostly-is bullying. Why most choose to overlook it? Honestly, the "why" of it is something I can't fathom. Is it too complex? Too ugly? Too sensitive? Too unsavory to be discussed? I like books that bring such topics to light, so I'm very sorry I couldn't like this wholly.<br><br><b>AND NOW MY REASONS</b><br><u>Elise is as judgemental as she is plastic. And it grates me like you wouldn't believe. </u> There's something to be said for reciprocation. If you don't want someone to judge you, start by not judging yourself. Elise bashes circular, popular music and musicians(granted, I'm no fan of circular music too but I am not offensive and mean about my opinions), calls all her classmates Idiots and says a lot more nonsense I won't bother trying to recall. Her voice sounded seriously offensive to me for most part of the book. It's okay to be angry and mad, maybe it's even the right thing to be, but it <b>did not go well at all with the pitiful and dispirited persona she was trying to sell.</b> She just felt too fake and manipulative for me. Is it even logical to complain about not having friends, about never being given a chance, about being made into a persona non grata, while on the side you dismiss the attempts of honest people, insult honest people who try to reach out to you<b> just because you consider them as social pariahs just like-and even worse than- you?</b> How different exactly are you from the people you curse? <br><br><b>I <u>needed</u> to understand why was she singled out in 4th grade. Why really? I mean in 4th grade? Just why?</b> It isn't impossible, yes I know, but the way it was presented in this book only came off as absurd to me. Maybe that's the root of it all, the presentation of her case failed me.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451367436ra/17534015.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Another problem I had was </b>I couldn't feel her pain at all. The thing that really didn't sit well with me was her attitude towards suicide: I get that Elise was shooting for humour, but It was just too breezy.<br><i>
  <blockquote>
<br>Plus I had spent so long on my playlist that it was already nearly five o’clock. So, realistically, this wasn’t a great day for dying. Which was a disappointment, but also sort of a relief. <br>Since I already had the X-Acto knife, though, and I already had the playlist, I decided to go into the bathroom to <b>practice a little. To practice cutting myself, I mean.</b> Just a little, so that when the time came to do it for real, it wouldn’t be scary. </blockquote>
</i><br>You're joking. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400997232ra/9745060.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And when she very logically meanders through different possible ways to do herself in, ticking several options off, so playfully, like it was a check list with groceries on it. I couldn't help but sing<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401086659ra/9754707.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Where are all the heartfelt emotions? <b>Seriously </b> I couldn't take the chick <b>seriously,</b> it was like she was trying too hard for pity, trying too, too hard to get my sympathy. For me, her voice lacked seriousness and the moving emotion which should easily be felt from someone who just decided to snap the thread connecting her to life. Her thoughts sounded more like analytical and experimental musings of a fascinated experimenter, a lot more than it did a broken, dispirited, and unrecoverable teenager. Therefore, I couldn't feel her pain.<br><br>And then she goes and says this:<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> Again, I knew I could look this up. How long does it take between the time you cut yourself and the time you die? The Internet would know. But I wouldn’t ask, because that made everything seem so clichéd. Another teenage suicide attempt, another cry for attention. It’s all been done before.<br> Only mine wasn’t going to be a cry for attention. </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><b>And it is all I can do to scream</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451364779ra/17533689.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386291847ra/7331023.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But as the book progresses, the story takes shape and she redeems herself<i> a little bit, in my opinion, </i>when she admits<br><br><i>"That’s what I discovered about myself on the first day of my sophomore year of high school: I didn’t really want to die. I never had. All I ever wanted was attention".</i><br><br>And I could only say: <b>And now I believe you. Let's start all over again. You're Elise, I'm Anne. This could be a good book.</b> And since I slept on it, I woke up feeling like<i> it was a good book, </i> though it never did become as affective as I hoped it would be. I loved the moments, rare as they were, when I connected with Elise, when I felt like I could understand her a little. When she said things like this:<br><i>
  <b>You can’t tell me my feelings are overwrought or absurd. You don’t know. They are my feelings. <br><br>I let them go. And then I leaned my head against the window and I cried.<br>Does this seem weak to you? Could you have done better? Fine, by all means, do better. But you don’t understand this: sometimes when you are worn down, day after day, relentlessly, with no reprieve for years piled on years, sometimes you lose everything but the ability to cry. <br><br>But I had no one who was really mine. </b>
</i><br><br>I loved her fervent love for music, I shared the moments of Joy music brought her.In general it's a good story, it's the specifics that keep biting me. But I don't regret reading it one bit, and I'd recommend it to anyone who wants to read a book that explores such subjects: <b>bullying, the power of music, the beauty and warmth of unexpected friendships, self discovery, romance and something like love(don't ask) </b>. It's the truth, it's a good story with a sound message. <br><b>Can we all just take a lesson from this sweet little darling here</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451364779ra/17533690.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="12744128175793688664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer935070970" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10062432896436369667">Disclaimer: I received a copy of this book for review from BookOutlet.ca in exchange for an honest review.<br/><br/>Elise.. The overachiever reminds me remarkably of me.. It's hilarious that she wanted to win at everything because I am the same way. If I start a new hobby, I want to learn everything about it so I can master it. Elise is the same way and I love that. She also doesn't know too much about social interactions, which is also something I don't know too well of. Her insightful mind and view of h</span>
  <span id="freeText10062432896436369667" style="display:none">Disclaimer: I received a copy of this book for review from BookOutlet.ca in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />Elise.. The overachiever reminds me remarkably of me.. It's hilarious that she wanted to win at everything because I am the same way. If I start a new hobby, I want to learn everything about it so I can master it. Elise is the same way and I love that. She also doesn't know too much about social interactions, which is also something I don't know too well of. Her insightful mind and view of herself and her world was just completely refreshing. Her demons were very similar to my demons and I'm certainly glad that she got through it. With the help of music and DJing, the title is completely literal and it saved her.<br /><br />I'm so wonderfully glad there's a teen character who felt real. She's not perfect at all, especially in the beginning when she attempts suicide. Some of the thoughts that she had felt realistic to someone who is going through depression. Being at such a low point in her life, you just wanted to hug her and tell her everything is going to be all right. <br /><br />Overall, a wonderful realistic read that you will definitely want to pick up. It's just that great and AHH I WANT EVERYONE TO READ IT. It's also the book that pretty much cemented me into enjoying contemporary.. *SHOCKED face*<br /><br />RATING 5/5<br /><br />QUOTES<br /><br />"I like that you're honest. Some girls might claim to be older, you know, so they seem more mature or whatever. You're not pretending to be anything you're not." (66)<br /><br />"I suck at pretending to be anything I'm not." (66)<br /><br />"I liked projects where I could take things apart and figure out exactly how they worked. The problem is, you can't do that with people." (70)<br /><br />"I can teach myself anything. Well, almost anything." (87)<br /><br />"Sometimes you just have those days where everything goes wrong. But sometimes, and totally unexpectedly, something can go right." (89)<br /><br />"There are some people who want to win at whatever they do, even if the things they do are not the sort of things one wins at." (106)<br /><br />"I don't need a makeover. I'm happy with myself the way I am." (114)<br /><br />"Who had don't this, and why? Who would possibly expend the time and energy just to hurt me this much?" (139)<br /><br />"I liked the idea of simply not having to be here anymore, not having to deal with life. As of death could be just an extended vacation." (145)<br /><br />"They're jealous of you because you're smart and you're talented and you know who you are." (154)<br /><br />"Popularity rewards the uninteresting." (206)<br /><br />"The world embraces ordinary. The world will never embrace you." (211)<br /><br />"Sometimes you have to give up something you are to get to who you want to be." (220)<br /><br />"Sometimes people think they know you. They know a few facts about you, and they piece you together in a way that makes sense to them. And if you don't know yourself very well, you might even believe that they are right. But the truth is, that it's you. That isn't you at all." (241)<br /><br />"People are who they are, try as you might, you cannot make them be what you want them to be." (271)<br /></span>

    <a title="Neil (or bleed)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14057379-neil-or-bleed"><img alt="Neil (or bleed)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572821192p2/14057379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/708486300?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neil (or bleed)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neil (or bleed)" href="/user/show/14057379-neil-or-bleed">Neil (or bleed)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14057379-neil-or-bleed?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer708486300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2082091661200239913"><blockquote>
  <i>I was broken<br/>I was choking<br/>I was lost<br/>This song saved my life<br/>I was bleeding<br/>Stopped believing<br/>Could have died<br/>This song saved my life<br/>I was down<br/>I was drowning<br/>But it came on just in time<br/>This song saved my life</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Simple Plan's This Song Saved My Life is the first thing I thought of, the first time I saw this novel. Now, that I have read this book, I can say that this song is relevant to the book.<br/><br/><br/><br/>I was ready to give this book 4 stars when I'm in a middle of reading it when the later part comes and I didn</span>
  <span id="freeText2082091661200239913" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>I was broken<br />I was choking<br />I was lost<br />This song saved my life<br />I was bleeding<br />Stopped believing<br />Could have died<br />This song saved my life<br />I was down<br />I was drowning<br />But it came on just in time<br />This song saved my life</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Simple Plan's This Song Saved My Life is the first thing I thought of, the first time I saw this novel. Now, that I have read this book, I can say that this song is relevant to the book.<br /><br /><br /><br />I was ready to give this book 4 stars when I'm in a middle of reading it when the later part comes and I didn't expect what I've got. No, it's not something shocking or mind-blowing but it's something hopeful, remarkable and truly heartwarming. It's like the unexplainable, pure joy I'm feeling when I'm seeing my family, my friends, and even myself happy despite everything. <br /><br />Oops! sorry it turned out to be I'm some kind of an emo but that's it. That's what I have experienced reading this wonderful novel. At least on the later part of the novel. Because, This Song Will Save Your Life isn't a happy book, in the first place. It carries a heavy package of emotions filled with sadness, worry, jealousy, and anger. In fact, this book started with a suicide attempt of the main character. She thinks her life doesn't make sense. She feels that she doesn't belong. So she changes herself forcefully; she tries to change herself but it doesn't change anything. At all.<br /><br />This Song Will Save Your Life is a powerful, profound and realistic novel that reminds us to be ourselves. It also reminds us that yeah, life is unfair, some people are just assholes. But, we have choices in life. We can choose to do what we really want and what make us happy. We can choose to not mind some people's judgment because at the end of the day, whether you do something or not, some people still have a say about you.<br /><br />Lastly, This Song Will Save Your Life has a special place now in my heart because I think it saved me, partly saved me from the nothing I've become (bring me to life). Lol!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2082091661200239913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2041281920" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2041281920" />
    <a title="WhatIReallyRead" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52500467-whatireallyread"><img alt="WhatIReallyRead" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483674713p2/52500467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2041281920?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="WhatIReallyRead" class="user" itemprop="url" name="WhatIReallyRead" href="/user/show/52500467-whatireallyread">WhatIReallyRead</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=hated">hated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=music">music</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2041281920" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2812321111019292223"><b>The reasons I debated giving it 2 stars instead of 1:</b><br/><br/>1) some cool songs were mentioned;<br/>2) reading the blurb, I had an inkling there was a strong chance I was going to hate it. I was rooting for the underdog, so to speak. So I feel like it's kind of on me.<br/><br/><b>The reasons I still ended up giving it 1 star</b> (spoilers ahead):<br/> <br/>Everything else.<br/><br/>1) <b>The heroine is both TSTL and the most awful, self-centered, petty and haughty person ever.</b> I just couldn't stand her. <br/><br/><b>So Elise wants to have friends and be popula</b></span>
  <span id="freeText2812321111019292223" style="display:none"><b>The reasons I debated giving it 2 stars instead of 1:</b><br /><br />1) some cool songs were mentioned;<br />2) reading the blurb, I had an inkling there was a strong chance I was going to hate it. I was rooting for the underdog, so to speak. So I feel like it's kind of on me.<br /><br /><b>The reasons I still ended up giving it 1 star</b> (spoilers ahead):<br /> <br />Everything else.<br /><br />1) <b>The heroine is both TSTL and the most awful, self-centered, petty and haughty person ever.</b> I just couldn't stand her. <br /><br /><b>So Elise wants to have friends and be popular. </b><br /><br />- A classmate (Amelia) asked to borrow her pen.<br />- Elise thinks: why not become friends with her? So she comes up to Amelia and her friends during lunch and sits with them.<br />- Since none of these people know her, have never spoken to her and didn't invite her, the girls talk about stuff that interests them. They are not being mean or exclude Elise, but the conversation doesn't revolve around her.<br />- Elise is, of course, shocked. Why aren't they explaining 10 years worth of inside jokes to her at once? <br />- When the girls ask Elise to clean up after lunch, what is the logical next step? <b>Of course, to try and kill herself.</b> Again, no one was being mean - the girls take turns cleaning up. As an imposter who derailed the conversation and demanded attention the whole time, it was only logical to ask Elise to do something in return. There was no bullying. No depression or trauma was leading up to this - just a summer full of reading gossip magazines. <b>This suicide attempt was a temper tantrum by an astoundingly self-absorbed person.</b><br />- After cutting herself, Elise does what? <b>Calls the girl who "caused" the suicide attempt to blame her while bleeding.</b> WTF. To call a 16-year old girl. A normal, friendly girl. Does Elise not understand how traumatic and fucked up this is? To have a stranger you have spoken to 1 time call you while dying of suicide?<br />- Amelia is a smart girl, so she calls the ambulance and Elise is rescued.<br />- And Elise proceeds to do what? <b>To hate Amelia for calling the ambulance, because that was "betrayal". WTF WTF WTF WTF</b> She throws death glares at Amelia for a year and expects <b>apologies</b> for the 911 call that saved her life. <br />I CAN'T EVEN.<br /><br />Another example. Elise's younger sister spends a month making a "poetry castle" as her school project, whatever that means. Right before the project is due when the whole family is asleep Elise comes and <b>violently destroys it</b>. Yes, she demolishes the school project her small sister put her heart, creativity and lots of effort in. <br /><br />Why? Wait for it... wait for it... oh, because Elise thinks <b>the poetry castle will prevent her little sister from becoming popular</b>. Because apparently, Elise is an expert on popularity. And because popularity is vital for 7 year-olds. When the sister sees the ruins of her project in the morning and is completely crestfallen and heart-broken, and parents look at Elise like "wtf girl", Elise can't wrap her head around the fact that <b>parents pity the little sister and not Elise</b> in this situation. Because it's obvious to Elise who the injured party is here. What a psycho.<br /><br />2) <b>Elise looks down her nose on everyone yet she spends the whole book bemoaning her lack of popularity and admiration from the public.</b> Case in point:<br /><br /><blockquote>"I have friends now. Surprise! Making friends is actually not that hard when you drop every single one of your standards. "</blockquote><br />She <b>thinks her friends are stupid, shallow and pathetic</b>. She characterizes them this way in her mind and also tells them as much on several occasions. And these are the people who like her, care about her and help her.<br /><br />When a guy asks Elise to go to prom she is shocked and disgusted and <b>scornfully refuses him. Why? Because he has acne</b>. What an asshole. Sure, an invitation from anyone other than a prince is an insult to Elise.<br /><br /><blockquote>"Popular music isn't interesting-bad, it was bad-bad."<br />"My favorite band in kindergarten was the Cure, because I liked their lyrics."</blockquote><br />She revels in having better taste than everyone else and dispises anyone who likes "mainstream". No, Elise, you didn't like Cure because you were so special. You liked them because your dad put them on. <br /><br /><blockquote>"I started speaking in sentences when I was a year old."</blockquote><br />She'll never let this go, will she? It's been a while since you were 1 y.o. Elise, you don't need to impart this info within the first minute of meeting a person. Also, the speed of speech development is individual and it's not your accomplishment or grounds for ego-inflation.<br /><br /><blockquote>Don’t be special.</blockquote><br />Elise spends a lot of the book thinking the root of her problem is her grandiosity. She's just better, smarter and more special than everyone else. That's why she's not popular. Mediocrity is celebrated. So she is torn over having to tone her genius down. Honey, I hate to tell you this, but Einstein and Austen and Mozart were celebrated because they were outstanding. No one celebrates or even notices mediocre people. You just aren't outstanding. <br /><br />3) <b>Elise finds a way to make everything about her, to turn everything into a major trial for her, conspired by the unfair world.</b> Case in point:<br /><br /><blockquote>"Mostly I feel bad for Sally and Chava, but sometimes I’m jealous of them. Their parents clearly screwed them up for life, or at least for high school, so they have someone to blame for their uncoolness. I don’t have that luxury. I can only blame myself."<br />"So when I asked my father for DJ equipment, Dad didn’t ask why. "</blockquote><br /><br />So. Let me get this straight for you. <b>Elise feels like a victim because she has great parents.</b> Yes, caring, affluent, functional adults who provide for all her wants and needs, pay attention and spend quality time with her. A good privileged family in the USA. What a trial indeed!<br /><br /><blockquote>"I was uncool by fourth grade."</blockquote><br />Show me a person who was cool in fourth grade. <br /><br /><blockquote>"I was born to be unpopular."</blockquote><br />The miracle of birth is also about being popular.<br /><br /><blockquote>I was smiling like a crazy person because I had just made a hundred people dance, I had just made a hundred people scream, I had just made a hundred people happy. I, Elise, using my own power, had made people happy.</blockquote><br />She didn't write this song. She didn't even perform it. She just pressed 1 button to put on a song (at this point Elise didn't even DJ) that's been popular for decades and people like it. Immediately in her head, she's the queen with a super-power. She never gets over her ability to "read the crowd" and "make people happy".<br /><br />4) <b>Girl-on-girl hate to show the triumph of the heroine. </b><br /><br />There was a rivalry for the attention of the romantic interest. The rival girl was, of course, much prettier, fashionable, stylish, out-going, not awkward, funny, amazing, long legs in high heels and all. The author made it very obvious how unlikely it was for our mousy heroine to defeat her. <br /><br />So much the sweeter was her triumph when the romantic interest picked the heroine, and the rival girl disintegrated before our very eyes. She lost all self-respect, made public scenes, started regularly drinking to the point of passing out, groveled for the romantic hero not to leave her, got caught by her parents and sent home, etc. Wow, way to go.<br /><br />5) But it doesn't end there. <b>The heroine triumphs and lords over everyone</b> who used to ignore or dislike her. <br /><br />According to this book, do you know who cares about 16-year-old DJs playing 80's music in Glendale, Rhode Island? Apparently, everyone. <br /><br />- She quickly becomes a celebrity in her town, gets into the newspaper. <br />- Popular kids at school whose attention she used to crave are now vying for HER attention. <br />- She gets the DJing spot that the person who taught her to DJ wanted but never got. Of course, the owner of the club has no problems illegally employing her and never checks the documents of this obvious minor.<br />- She makes the career of her wannabe musician friends by inviting them to play in the club during her spot. They, of course, kill it. Thanks to her, but still.<br /><br />The list could go on and on, the point is, <b>the world is at her feet. Because that's what happens when you throw tantrums and openly scorn everyone - you conquer the world.</b><br /><br /><b>YUCK<b></b></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2812321111019292223" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1755264186" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1755264186" />
    <a title="ambsreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads"><img alt="ambsreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508924675p2/30813900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1755264186?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ambsreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ambsreads" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads">ambsreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1755264186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5487667298241533416"><b>3.5 stars<br/><br/>TRIGGER WARNINGS: self-harm, suicidal thoughts, and bullying.</b><br/><br/><i>This Song Will Save Your Life</i> was a book I had never come across or even thought about until I watched Emmmabooks video <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xWmkXBfuR4g' rel='nofollow noopener'>I Am The Reader Book Tag</a>. She started to talk about it in the review and before she had even finished I'd got the book. I couldn't stop myself. The concept behind the book was something that would have meant so much to me when I was younger and struggling with my depression and anxiety (without even knowing I</span>
  <span id="freeText5487667298241533416" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars<br><br>TRIGGER WARNINGS: self-harm, suicidal thoughts, and bullying.</b><br><br><i>This Song Will Save Your Life</i> was a book I had never come across or even thought about until I watched Emmmabooks video <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xWmkXBfuR4g" rel="nofollow noopener">I Am The Reader Book Tag</a>. She started to talk about it in the review and before she had even finished I'd got the book. I couldn't stop myself. The concept behind the book was something that would have meant so much to me when I was younger and struggling with my depression and anxiety (without even knowing I was). It was a book that made me cry and feel sadness for the main character Elise. <br><br><b>Elise</b> is a character who has been unpopular her whole life. She doesn't know why. She's different and because of that kids have latched onto that. It was sad to read about how Elise was treated and her mindset, however, it was absolutely believable was incredible. Becoming who she is, with the help of music, and realising she is worthy of having loving friendships and family. That she isn't alone. It was a journey of growth that was incredibly heartbreaking but ended up being a beautiful book. <br><br>Of course, I had some problems with the book. The writing style was amazing, and I did only cringe a few times. The first time? Here. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Do you want to dance?" he asked, holding out his hand to me. <br>"I wanna dance with somebody," Whitney sang, "with somebody who loves me."<br>I shook my head, feeling myself blush. "I don't really dance."<br>Char furrowed his brow. "Why not?"<br>"I ... I don't really know how."</i>
</blockquote> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473910983ra/20529872.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I couldn't help it. It was such a cliche scene that had me cringing so much.<br><br>The second time? During Char and Elise's 'relationship', I couldn't refrain from feeling uncomfortable at a relationship shared between a 16-year-old and a 20-year-old. As someone who is closer to the age of 20 (<i>oh lord I'm 20 next year</i>) than that of 16 I couldn't imagine how it happened. That's not to say it doesn't happen, but I just felt it wasn't quite necessary for the overall plot. <br><br>However, despite my low rating, this book has become one of my favourites. The overall messages within this book - that high school doesn't matter at the end of the day and that things <b>do</b> get better. This makes this book an important book, a book that would be good for teenagers currently struggling. Or anyone. The writing style makes it enjoyable and the overall story is enjoyable, I didn't even mind the open ending in this case. <br><br>Overall? A really good book, I highly recommend it. I'm also glad it didn't join my ever growing DNF pile. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473911634ra/20529941.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="5487667298241533416" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1383592914" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1383592914" />
    <a title="Jenny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38962215-jenny"><img alt="Jenny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583924348p2/38962215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1383592914?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny" href="/user/show/38962215-jenny">Jenny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447252832" href="/book/show/18114890-this-song-will-save-your-life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38962215-jenny?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38962215-jenny?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38962215-jenny?shelf=inspirational">inspirational</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38962215-jenny?shelf=emotional-read">emotional-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38962215-jenny?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38962215-jenny?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1383592914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer766198722900358105"><b>“Sometimes people think they know you. They know a few facts about you, and they piece you together in a way that makes sense to them. And if you don't know yourself very well, you might even believe that they are right. But the truth is, that isn't you. That isn't you at all.” </b><br/><br/>This isn't a kind of book that will keep you at the edge of your seat, or keep surprising you with plot twists; it's just a simple story about a girl who has never been popular in her life, does all the silly things teena</span>
  <span id="freeText766198722900358105" style="display:none"><b>“Sometimes people think they know you. They know a few facts about you, and they piece you together in a way that makes sense to them. And if you don't know yourself very well, you might even believe that they are right. But the truth is, that isn't you. That isn't you at all.” </b><br /><br />This isn't a kind of book that will keep you at the edge of your seat, or keep surprising you with plot twists; it's just a simple story about a girl who has never been popular in her life, does all the silly things teenagers does-some quite serious,too, but somehow it also inspires you and manages to leave a very strong impression. This is my second book by the author, and the thing I love most about her books is how well crafted and flawed her characters are that even such simple story could mean so much. Her simplistic writing and the way she handles such serious issues like bullying and suicide takes her books to the another level.<br /><br />This book is from a perspective of Elise, who has never been famous in her life, has always been kind of a person who sits away from the 'cool' group, and not because she doesn't like them, because she feels like she could never fit in that cool group. The first half is basically Elise trying to become one of the cool kids, and for that she even had a list of things she was supposed to do. She also attempts suicide, just to get attention. And while I do not agree with that sort of thing, or in any way can come up with an excuse for her behavior-because it's just wrong, I've also heard about real life incidents like these around me, so as stupid as may sounds, people actually do this. But that didn't stop me from loving the book, because thankfully, that was only a small part of the book, and the rest of the book is actually very interesting and fun when we get to know about this underground Dj party, which in some way changes Elise's life.<br /><br /><br />The other issue in this book was bullying. When Elise was trying to build a new life with music, there was also something going on in her life that just didn't fit and made her life much more difficult. She was bullied constantly, and even though she said things she wasn't supposed to, I could actually relate to her. I wasn't bullied in high school, but I also wasn't the person anyone would consider to be fun and would hang out with. I was the kid who sat alone with few of her friends and just noticed people around her doing fun things which she wasn't able to do. So in that matter, this book really did touched me more than I could have imagined. And even the end of the book was somehow very similar to my life which just made this book more special. <br /><br />Then there were secondary characters who made this book more fun to read. I loved Elise's family and her cute siblings, her bitchy <i> and</i> supportive friends, and yes, I also loved Char. Okay, not so much at the end, but overall I really liked his character. It was really nice to see how Elise realized at the end who her real friends were and how she was wrong about so many things in her life. Elise also had the habit of judging people without even listening to them, and that I think ruined many things on the way- because she won't believe anyone. The characters I will remember most are VIkki, Harry, Mel, and Char. There were also some characters whom I actually started liking at the end, when everything was sorted out. <br /><br />I also like how this book had a bit of mystery going on, just like in <i> Tonight The Streets Are Ours </i>, and how it was handled at the end. Though the ending wasn't dramatic or anything, in fact I never really got emotional while reading the book, everything just kind of made sense at the end. The ending was very real, too. In real life not everything happens the way you want it to be, and this showed exactly that. I liked how everything didn't end happily with Elise's life, and that's because life isn't always pretty, but I also loved how some characters did get what they deserved,<br /><br />It was a great, uplifting read for me. I can say that this book is either a hit or miss for people. But I am a kind of person who loves a story which gives a strong message, even if it not might be the most exciting book I've read, because I know that despite being simple, it was worth reading. <br />even if you're not like Elise, I'm sure you could relate to her somehow, and I would definitely recommend this book to everyone. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="766198722900358105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_678344138" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/678344138" />
    <a title="Beatrice Masaluñga" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga"><img alt="Beatrice Masaluñga" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603719912p2/4590441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/678344138?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beatrice Masaluñga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beatrice Masaluñga" href="/user/show/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga">Beatrice Masaluñga</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250050748" href="/book/show/21469098-this-song-will-save-your-life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer678344138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13061096702283878425"><i>This Song Will Save Your Life</i> hits my heart in the rawest way. The story was so realistic and straightforward. The lines were so relatable and I don't know how to describe what I'm feeling right now as my emotions swirled all over me. I'll make this as a short review because it's hard to formulate a review for this book. <br/><br/><b>Elise Dembowski is an easy character to sympathize with. </b> In her school, she's been bullied and treated as an outcast. She wants a sense of belonging or just fit in on a crowd. </span>
  <span id="freeText13061096702283878425" style="display:none"><i>This Song Will Save Your Life</i> hits my heart in the rawest way. The story was so realistic and straightforward. The lines were so relatable and I don't know how to describe what I'm feeling right now as my emotions swirled all over me. I'll make this as a short review because it's hard to formulate a review for this book. <br /><br /><b>Elise Dembowski is an easy character to sympathize with. </b> In her school, she's been bullied and treated as an outcast. She wants a sense of belonging or just fit in on a crowd. She tried to commit suicide for being treated badly but through music, it became her therapy. She becomes a DJ at a nightclub where people can see her for who she is. Someone who's vibrant and passionate about music. I remember the feeling of not being able to fit in a crowd when I was in high school. There was a time I really felt invisible during a conversation and when I tried to join in, they just continued as if I weren't there with them. It hurts and I felt lonely. I also remembered having a heart-to-heart talk with my mom about it. She said that I should cheer up and do things I enjoyed like playing Badminton or reading a book. That's what I did and in the end, I found a few friends whom I'm comfortable with and accept me for who I am. Until now, I still keep in touch with them. <br /><br /><b>What lesson did I learn from this book? </b> You don't have to change just to fit in the crowd. Just be yourself and enjoy what you're passionate about. You'll find a group of friends who'll accept you for who you are. Who will be there when you needed through good and bad times. <br /><br />Can I say this book has an impeccable list of songs? For someone who enjoys old tunes, I appreciate it very much. I love listening to them all. <br /><br />Final rating: 4.5 / 5 stars<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13061096702283878425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2004006453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2004006453" />
    <a title="Julie Zantopoulos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51094260-julie-zantopoulos"><img alt="Julie Zantopoulos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503178209p2/51094260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2004006453?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie Zantopoulos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie Zantopoulos" href="/user/show/51094260-julie-zantopoulos">Julie Zantopoulos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250050748" href="/book/show/21469098-this-song-will-save-your-life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51094260-julie-zantopoulos?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51094260-julie-zantopoulos?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2004006453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9233194136901398383">This book has been on my TBR shelf for so damned long! I was anticipating it and really thought it would be a five star read but something just didn't sit right with me. I enjoyed it, but it wasn't a blow me out of the water great read. <br/><br/><i>"...you are still, always, you: beautiful and brushed, known and unknowable..."</i><br/><br/>This book centers around Elise who is living split between her divorced parent's houses and under their watchful eyes after an attempted suicide left her family shaken up. Unable to sl</span>
  <span id="freeText9233194136901398383" style="display:none">This book has been on my TBR shelf for so damned long! I was anticipating it and really thought it would be a five star read but something just didn't sit right with me. I enjoyed it, but it wasn't a blow me out of the water great read. <br /><br /><i>"...you are still, always, you: beautiful and brushed, known and unknowable..."</i><br /><br />This book centers around Elise who is living split between her divorced parent's houses and under their watchful eyes after an attempted suicide left her family shaken up. Unable to sleep at night Elise wanders the streets of her town until she comes across an underground dance club, a few friends, and a charasmatic DJ. Now, Elise has something to look forward to at the end of each day...losing herself in the music and the crowd. <br /><br />Elise struggles to read social cues and understand the intricacies of the social scene. Making friends isn't easy for her, fitting in is difficult, and she feels like there's nowhere that she belongs and nobody who she belongs to. That's further made difficult when the people she surrounds herself with are all hiding their own secrets and have their own reasons for behaving the way they are. But, at the end of the day, having parents who love her but still fail to realize that she's out until 4am most nights seems so unbelievable. Having her act like a total ass to her half-sister is just crappy. There were things that she did that just failed to make sense to me and plot points that were way too convenient. <br /><br />I think that Char can get kicked right in his dick. Just saying...not charming, at all. Also, there's a weird vibe of pedophilia that takes place in this book because Char and Elise enter into a physical relationship and he's 19 going on 20 and she's 16. Normally, that kind of a 3 year age gap wouldn't bother me but she stresses to him over and over and OVER that she's 16. He even says at one point that he likes that she's 16. Which is just gross. And there's a lot of reminding that she's underage and he's...not! So, you know, that's pretty damn gross. <br /><br />But, I did enjoy the book overall...so take what I say with a grain of salt. I mean, I'm probably the last person to read this book, anyway. <br /><br />Trigger warnings for self-harm, cutting, attempted suicide, sex with a minor, discussion of an eating disorder (bulimia), binge drinking, and cyberbullying. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9233194136901398383" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1797161661" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1797161661" />
    <a title="Caitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57334157-caitlin"><img alt="Caitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507948675p2/57334157.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1797161661?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caitlin" href="/user/show/57334157-caitlin">Caitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1797161661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4737316957287320395">I am honestly very torn as to what rating this book deserves. There are a lot of powerful messages in this book so I think I'll keep it at a 3.5-4 star rating. <br/><br/><i>This is going to be a semi-personal review so I'm sorry if they're not your thing!</i><br/><br/>This was a really easy book to relate to. I've been in the position of almost all of the characters in the book throughout different times of my life. Even some aspects that I couldn't directly relate to, I have witnessed my friends follow the same path that</span>
  <span id="freeText4737316957287320395" style="display:none">I am honestly very torn as to what rating this book deserves. There are a lot of powerful messages in this book so I think I'll keep it at a 3.5-4 star rating. <br /><br /><i>This is going to be a semi-personal review so I'm sorry if they're not your thing!</i><br /><br />This was a really easy book to relate to. I've been in the position of almost all of the characters in the book throughout different times of my life. Even some aspects that I couldn't directly relate to, I have witnessed my friends follow the same path that Elise took. My best friend used to walk the streets every single night because he was searching for so many answers that he couldn't find anywhere else but out in the streets at night. He never found an underground nightclub like Elise did but I think he did find some of the answers he was looking for.<br /><br /><i>
  <b> "Sometimes when you are worn down, day after day, relentlessly, with no reprieve for years piled on years, sometimes you lose everything but the ability to cry" </b>
</i> <br /><br />Honestly this quote hits me so hard. I, like many other people, have experienced my fair share of bullying. It was never to the extreme that Elise suffered in this novel but for about 2 years I dreaded going to school because my "friends" turned on me and decided to make my life a living hell. For about 6 months I got off the school bus in the morning and would sit in the bathroom and hide so I wouldn't have to deal with anyone. I spent a long time jumping between friendship groups because no one really wanted to sit with me. <br /><br />Elise's journey with suicidal thoughts and self harm was limited in comparison to the journey that I know a lot of people have travelled (I myself have travelled along that path). However, it was very real and raw. There's one section when a girl tells her she did it wrong because she didn't cut herself the right way to die. Elise replies to this and says no I didn't. I'm not entirely sure if this is what the author meant but from my experience, you don't harm yourself to die, you hurt yourself to live. Even when Elise was planning on committing suicide, she didn't want to die. She wanted to end the life she was currently living. She just wanted someone else's life. In a way she did do that even though she didn't go through with her suicide attempt because she got the life that she wanted. <br /><br />Elise's journey with bullying was heartbreaking to read about. It is mentioned in this book that she was picked in fourth grade as the target for all sorts of bullying. It's horrible to admit but I remember this happening in school. There was 1 girl who was the target of lots of bullying but no one ever really stood up for her. It's tough reading something like this because you realise how much you could have helped them if only you paid attention more or put in the effort to care. I feel like almost all of us will be guilty of doing the exact same thing.<br /><br /><i> <b>"Sometimes people think they know you. They know a few facts about you, and they piece you together in a way that makes sense to them. And if you don't know yourself very well, you might even believe that they are right. But the truth is, that isn't you. That isn't you at all."</b></i><br /><br />This quote hit me even harder. I feel like this could be used to sum up the majority of my life and I'm sure a lot of people could also relate to this. I'm going to end my review here on this extremely powerful quote. At the end of the day you can try and change yourself 200 times to become someone that other people will 'like' but it will only hurt yourself. There's nothing worse than being trapped inside yourself. <br /><br /><i>
  <b> "You think it's so easy to change yourself. You think it's so easy but it's not. True, things don't stay the same forever: couches are replaced, boys leave, you discover a song, your body becomes forever scarred. And with each of these moments you change and change again, your true self spinning, shifting positions - but at last it returns to you, like a dancer on the floor. Because throughout it all, you are still, always, you: beautiful and bruised, known and unknowable. And isn't that - just you - enough?" </b>
</i> <br /><br />Always remember: your scars are what make you, you. You are beautiful even with your battle scars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4737316957287320395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
